             <div class="fauxborder-right">
             </div>
             <div class="fauxcolumn-inner">

               <div class="widget Blog" data-version="1" id="Blog1">
                <div class="blog-posts hfeed">
                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Monday, June 11, 2018
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="5743258563765251847" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="5743258563765251847">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2018/06/lightning-to-children-eased-with.html">
                       Lightning to the Children eased With explanation kind
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-5743258563765251847" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Dickenson:
                      </div>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq" style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Tell all the Truth but tell it slant --
                       <br/>
                       Success in Circuit lies
                       <br/>
                       Too bright for our infirm Delight
                       <br/>
                       The Truth's superb surprise
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq" style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; padding: 0px;'>
                       As Lightning to the Children eased
                       <br/>
                       With explanation kind
                       <br/>
                       The Truth must dazzle gradually
                       <br/>
                       Or every man be blind --
                      </blockquote>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; padding: 0px;'>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Karl Popper:
                      </div>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq" style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Less well known is the paradox of tolerance: Unlimited tolerance must lead to the disappearance of tolerance. If we extend unlimited tolerance even to those who are intolerant, if we are not prepared to defend a tolerant society against the onslaught of the intolerant, then the tolerant will be destroyed, and tolerance with them. — In this formulation, I do not imply, for instance, that we should always suppress the utterance of intolerant philosophies; as long as we can counter them by rational argument and keep them in check by public opinion, suppression would certainly be unwise.
                       <b>
                        But we should claim the right to suppress them if necessary even by force; for it may easily turn out that they are not prepared to meet us on the level of rational argument, but begin by denouncing all argument; they may forbid their followers to listen to rational argument, because it is deceptive, and teach them to answer arguments by the use of their fists or pistols.
                       </b>
                       We should therefore claim, in the name of tolerance, the right not to tolerate the intolerant.
                      </blockquote>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Emphasis mine.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       When facts are thrown out, there is no way to convince anyone of the truth. And if what those who can't be convinced are doing is as horrible as what these people are doing, then how are we going to stop them? With an election? LOL.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       It's the age-old MLK vs Malcolm X argument. And here's where MLK wound up on that:
                      </div>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq" style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       I must confess that over the past few years I have been gravely disappointed with the white moderate. I have almost reached the regrettable conclusion that the Negro’s great stumbling block in his stride toward freedom is not the White Citizen’s Counciler or the Ku Klux Klanner, but the white moderate, who is more devoted to “order” than to justice; who prefers a negative peace which is the absence of tension to a positive peace which is the presence of justice; who constantly says: “I agree with you in the goal you seek, but I cannot agree with your methods of direct action”; who paternalistically believes he can set the timetable for another man’s freedom; who lives by a mythical concept of time and who constantly advises the Negro to wait for a “more convenient season.”
                      </blockquote>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Now think about that from the perspective of a parent who came here seeking an asylum from a drug war that is
                       <b>
                        our fault
                       </b>
                       and who had their kid ripped away from them, and then go down there and patiently tell them that we have to dazzle hateful, willfully ignorant monsters who are kidnapping their children
                       <em style="border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; font-family: inherit; line-height: 1; margin: 0px; padding: 0px;">
                        gradually
                       </em>
                       .
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; padding: 0px;'>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-footer">

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Friday, May 25, 2018
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="8425374089242920764" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="8425374089242920764">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2018/05/liberals-need-to-stop-pretending-that.html">
                       Liberals Need to Stop Pretending that Being Nice to These People Will Make Them Listen
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-8425374089242920764" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Trump is out of control. He's destroying norms and institutions that have held this country together for centuries. He attacks people viciously while the conservatives and libertarians cheer him on. They laugh about it. They think it's awesome to make liberals cry. The night of the election, they were literally making fun of anyone who cried. Liberal tears, yadda yadda. He has infected these people with his venom, and now they viciously go after people they disagree with. They have attacked me in ways I've never attacked them. And then they're snowflakes if you dare to even approach their level of viciousness with mere words.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Because that is who they are. That is what they do. They are vicious people who cheer on war or care so much more about tax cuts and forcing women to give birth that even if they don't like war they just shrug it off and make the false equivalence that Dems are just as bad. They put forward policy prescriptions that aren't abstract thoughts; they're horrible actions that affect people's lives in horrible ways. When people say shit like that--tell us that they want our country to do horrible stuff--then being nice to them only enables them. It normalizes them. When they lie, and we say that's unconfirmed or that's questionable, we only enable them to lie more.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       We need to call lies lies. We need to say that something horrible is horrible. When they say that "stealing" their money is horrible, they're full of shit. It's not theft, it's the price you pay to live in the greatest country on earth. And when you say you don't care about anything but getting a tax cut, you are
                       <b>
                        literally
                       </b>
                       saying
                       <b>
                        FUCK YOU
                       </b>
                       to all the people who will suffer because you cut the things that make us civilized, the things that keep old people from starving or freezing, that keep young people from being so hungry they can't learn. I have shown them how universal health care would save us money, they don't care. I have shown them that investing in infrastructure will save us money and bring jobs home, they don't care. I've shown them how having an educated populace makes us stronger and richer, they don't care. I've shown them that immigrants make us stronger, commit crime at lower rates, provide a workforce that Americans don't want to be in, they don't care. I've shown them that minorities do drugs at the same rate as whites but are about 8 times as likely to get busted for it... They. Don't. Care.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Even if you show them how supposed conservative goals, like debt reduction, can be better achieved through investing in people and infrastructure, they don't care. If a liberal thought of it, it must be wrong. I see liberals trying to bend over backward, like Obama did with O-care, with almost giving up chained CPI, and what did he get for it? Donald Trump spreading racist rumors about him not even being an American. He got more hatred from the right than any other Democratic President since FDR, despite the fact that he was the most moderate Democrat in modern history.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       I've tried to show these things to them by being nice. When I was younger, I thought I could be persuasive with speech. What I learned is that if you win an argument with them, they get quite angry and go directly for the personal attacks and threats of physical harm. I've actually found that former conservatives with whom I used to argue vigorously were impressed that a liberal would stand up to them like that. Some of them, due to the Iraq war, now vote for Democrats. One of them is now a sober Buddhist who has thanked me for changing his life. We used to get in each other's faces over this shit. He said my willingness to stand up to his old self and the barrage he could throw (this is a very tough Biker/ mercenary stagehand friend--you know who you are) impressed him enough to consider what I said more carefully.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Now if you guys all want to play footsie with these accomplices to mass murderers and fraudsters and racists and child starvers, you go right ahead. But you're not going to get anywhere, just like I haven't. The only thing they care about is making liberals cry. Or making liberals mad. As long as they get their tax cuts, they don't give a fuck about anyone else. We're all lazy or stupid to them; there's no such thing as bad luck in their world. There's no racism to ruin the lives of minorities, just stupid minorities. There are no accidents that are beyond people's control, just lazy people who don't want to work. There's no bad luck, or lead in the water, or pesticides the EPA lets be used even though they're proven to make people stupid. There's literally nothing that ever happens in this world that you didn't bring on yourself.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       They cheer for our
                       <a href="http://goodtogocv.com/">
                        family business
                       </a>
                       to fail, even though we are literally doing the thing they say liberals don't do. We make our community a better place. We work hard. We support our local farmers, serve healthy food that makes our people healthier. And what do we get for all this? We get ridiculed. I hear jokes about how much our place must suck, how we're doomed to fail... It's so sickeningly hypocritical and counterproductive.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       They have no empathy. Their arguments are just a big pile of puke covered fallacies and vicious threats when they can no longer argue. But please, go right ahead and play nice. I can't wait to see the frustration that will result from trying to reason with anyone who would vote for Donny T or Roy Moore or any of the other piles of fat and hubris that pass themselves off as anything other than the hatemongers they are.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       If any of you really think you can convince people to not support Trump by being nice to them, then go for it. I feel the same way about you being nice to them as you feel about me being mean.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       I've lived through Nixon, Reagan, Bush, Bush II, and now this. I've seen a lot of bad shit happen, like Reagan joking about gay people dying of AIDS while he did nothing about it. Like W killing a million people and blowing trillions of dollars on a war of lies. Like Republicans cutting funds to even study gun violence, or not doing anything to protect children in school. Nobody ever stopped anything like that by being nice. There comes a time when you have to stand up and call this shit what it is: unacceptable. There comes a time when vicious thugs who promote deadly bullshit have to be called out and fought in the streets if necessary. Too many people hide from these things, hate the confrontation, don't want to get involved. If we're nice, then all the horrible shit gets swept under a rug instead of splayed out in the public square for everyone to see.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; margin-bottom: 15px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Read MLK's letters from the Birmingham jail. Realize what he realized: that the moderate afraid of confrontation because they prefer "peace" and "order" (for themselves, of course, but not for those suffering) over justice is the bigger problem. It's time to stand up to these people. Do it nicely, fine, whatever, but stop taking shit. Stand up for what you believe in. Do what you think will make the world better. You might think that what I'm doing doesn't help, fine, I think the same of you. But it's going to take all of us doing what we think is right to change anything, and it's going to take all of us attacking the worst of them head-on.
                      </div>
                      <div style='border: 0px; box-sizing: border-box; color: #2a2e2e; font-family: "Helvetica Neue", arial, sans-serif; font-size: 15px; line-height: 21px; padding: 0px;'>
                       Now I'm exhausted. I'm old, in constant pain, and still doing my best to leave the world better than I found it. If you made it through this whole tirade, I thank you. Now get out there and get in someone's face that deserves it. Don't be scared. Stick your chin out. Let them take a swing. You'll love yourself in the morning for it.
                      </div>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Wednesday, November 09, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="8941996452304638259" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="8941996452304638259">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2016/11/an-interminable-succession-of.html">
                       An Interminable Succession of Absurdities Imposed by the Myopic Logic of Short-term Thinking
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-8941996452304638259" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      Trump lead in MI: 16,701. Votes for Stein: 51,103. Votes for Johnson: 171,699.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Trump lead in WI: 26,889. Votes for Stein: 30,957. Votes for Johnson: 106,292.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Trump lead in PA: 68,012. Votes for Stein: 48,998. Votes for Johnson: 142,625.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Trump lead in AZ: 81,607. Votes for Stein: 22,734. Votes for Johnson: 72,183.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      "We are living in an interminable succession of absurdities imposed by the myopic logic of short-term thinking."—Jacques-Yves Cousteau
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                      What happens to bullshitting narcissists who lose the interest of their sycophants?
                      <br/>
                      <div>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div>
                       <script src="//www.google.com/trends/embed.js?hl=en-US&amp;q=/m/0cqt90,+/m/07j6ty,+/m/0dpr5f,+/m/02zzm_&amp;geo=US-NH&amp;date=now+7-d&amp;cmpt=q&amp;tz=Etc/GMT%2B5&amp;tz=Etc/GMT%2B5&amp;content=1&amp;cid=TIMESERIES_GRAPH_AVERAGES_CHART&amp;export=5&amp;w=600&amp;h=400" type="text/javascript">

                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Thursday, July 16, 2015
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="1948344345770676643" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="1948344345770676643">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2015/07/jeb-bullshits-on-how-republicans-win.html">
                       Jeb! Bullshits on How Republicans Win Elections
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-1948344345770676643" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      While looking at how his lack of understanding of The Donald could be leading Jeb! to trouble,
                      <a href="http://www.boomantribune.com/story/2015/7/16/1354/47628">
                       Booman notes a quote from Jeb
                      </a>
                      !
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       “A Republican will never win by striking fear in people’s hearts.”-Jeb! Bush
                      </blockquote>
                      <br/>
                      Silly, Jeb! That's the only way Republicans win. To wit:
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "Our enemies are innovative and resourceful, and so are we. They never stop thinking about new ways to harm our country and our people, and neither do we."--GW Bush, Aug 5, 2004
                      </blockquote>
                      <div>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://ws-na.amazon-adsystem.com/widgets/q?_encoding=UTF8&amp;ASIN=0743254783&amp;Format=_SL250_&amp;ID=AsinImage&amp;MarketPlace=US&amp;ServiceVersion=20070822&amp;WS=1&amp;tag=scottsupakbaldmo" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="3893668204765534181" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="3893668204765534181">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2015/04/if-nate-silver-ignores-emerging.html">
                       If Nate Silver Ignores the Emerging Democratic Majority I Hope His Readers are Betting On It
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-3893668204765534181" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0743254783/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0743254783&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=scottsupakbaldmo&amp;linkId=FNJFBHXF7VUQDESO" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;">
                       <img border="0" height="200" src="http://ws-na.amazon-adsystem.com/widgets/q?_encoding=UTF8&amp;ASIN=0743254783&amp;Format=_SL250_&amp;ID=AsinImage&amp;MarketPlace=US&amp;ServiceVersion=20070822&amp;WS=1&amp;tag=scottsupakbaldmo" width="129"/>
                      </a>
                      <img alt="" border="0" height="1" src="http://ir-na.amazon-adsystem.com/e/ir?t=scottsupakbaldmo&amp;l=as2&amp;o=1&amp;a=0743254783" style="border: none !important; margin: 0px !important;" width="1"/>
                      Nate Silver has dipped his toe into the 2016 Presidential prediction market with some typical horse race bullshit that papers over a few key points.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       As Sean Trende has pointed out, it relies on a selective reading of the evidence — emphasizing 2012, 2008 and 2006 but ignoring 2014, 2010, and 2004.
                      </blockquote>
                      14 and 10 are midterms, when the emerging demographic nightmare for the GOP stayed home. 2004 was way back on the demographic curve, and it was a warmongering year when the GOP used gay marriage as a wedge to get their voters out. And even then, Bush barely won.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <a href="http://www.pewhispanic.org/files/2012/11/hispanic-2012-11-07-latino-vote-00-02.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em; text-align: center;">
                        <br/>
                       </a>
                       Perhaps more important, predictions made on the premise of “emerging” majorities have a miserable track record: Republicans were bragging about their “permanent” majority in 2004, for instance, only to get their butts kicked in 2006 and 2008.
                      </blockquote>
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.pewhispanic.org/files/2012/11/hispanic-2012-11-07-latino-vote-00-02.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" src="http://www.pewhispanic.org/files/2012/11/hispanic-2012-11-07-latino-vote-00-02.png"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.pewhispanic.org/2012/11/07/latino-voters-in-the-2012-election/">
                           From Pew Research Center
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Republicans might not have gotten their butts kicked if they hadn't lied us into a $2 trillion (borrowed) war and crashed the economy into the Little Bush Depression. They really might have had a better chance if they'd passed immigration reform.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      However, this still ignores the surge in minority voters, especially Latinos, and especially in swing states, or previously red states like AZ that will gradually turn blue as long as Republicans keep hating on minorities.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      And this is the important part. The sliver of the GOP that wants immigration reform, or sentencing reform, or any other logical "outreach" to minorities will be crushed by the xenophobic base that votes in primaries.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      It's a real problem for them, and to shrug it off with such a condescending brush off reveals a lack of understanding of the facts behind the actual demographic theory.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      So, comparing Democratic claims of an emerging majority to Republican claims isn't really fair. The GOP was bullshitting. They had nothing to base their claims of an emerging majority on. Democrats actually do. See the original book on the subject,
                      <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0743254783/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0743254783&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=scottsupakbaldmo&amp;linkId=EEXZNUEH77IRZMGL">
                       <i>
                        The Emerging Democratic Majority
                       </i>
                      </a>
                      <img alt="" border="0" height="1" src="http://ir-na.amazon-adsystem.com/e/ir?t=scottsupakbaldmo&amp;l=as2&amp;o=1&amp;a=0743254783" style="border: none !important; margin: 0px !important;" width="1"/>
                      , by John Judis and Ruy Teixeira.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      But, hey, Nate, at least
                      <a href="http://predictit.org/">
                       we can bet on it
                      </a>
                      at Predict It, where a Democrat is currently
                      <a href="https://www.predictit.org/Home/SingleMarket?marketId=1296">
                       a 56% favorite to win the White House
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <div>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                       <a href="http://www.pewhispanic.org/files/2012/11/hispanic-2012-11-07-latino-vote-00-02.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;">
                        <br/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Tuesday, January 27, 2015
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-OOMpyOvt_KI/VMhGUhugkKI/AAAAAAAAIwY/lJikbDhnqBs/s1600/family_income_median_income_growth_productivity1.png" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="1639527514479202367" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="1639527514479202367">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2015/01/the-large-print-giveth-and-small-print.html">
                       The Large Print Giveth and the Small Print Taketh Away
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-1639527514479202367" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-OOMpyOvt_KI/VMhGUhugkKI/AAAAAAAAIwY/lJikbDhnqBs/s1600/family_income_median_income_growth_productivity1.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="288" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-OOMpyOvt_KI/VMhGUhugkKI/AAAAAAAAIwY/lJikbDhnqBs/s1600/family_income_median_income_growth_productivity1.png" width="400"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          Things were different back in Lil' Johnny's day.
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Speaker Boehner bullshits on 60 Minutes:
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       I’ve had every kinda rotten job you can imagine growin’ up and gettin’ myself through school. And I wouldn’t have had a chance at half those jobs if the federal government had kept imposing [a] higher minimum wage.
                      </blockquote>
                      OK, 60 Minutes, you're journalists. You should be ready for that question. If Scott Pelley is too chicken shit to follow up with the obvious facts that prove the Speaker is bullshitting, then maybe your ratings would go up if you hired someone who could....
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Here's
                      <a href="http://www.msnbc.com/rachel-maddow-show/boehner-undermines-his-own-minimum-wage-argument">
                       Steve Benen
                      </a>
                      :
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Boehner expressed relief that the government didn’t keep “imposing” a higher minimum wage at the time, but in reality, the government actually did keep “imposing” a higher minimum wage, raising in 1974, 1975, and again in 1976 – just as Boehner was working through college.
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       And adjusted for inflation, those minimum wages had greater purchasing power than the minimum wage now.
                      </blockquote>
                      Now, was that so hard?
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Too bad all those old folks at home just nodded along with the Speaker while Scott Pelley moved on to the next question.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Too bad all those old folks will never know the
                      <a href="http://www.peri.umass.edu/fileadmin/pdf/working_papers/working_papers_351-400/WP373.pdf">
                       real math
                      </a>
                      : "...if the federal minimum wage had risen in step with both inflation and average labor productivity since 1968, the federal minimum today would be $25.50 an hour."
                      <br/>
                      <div>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">

                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="7444455625812656148" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="7444455625812656148">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2014/12/the-cost-shifting-of-negative.html">
                       The Cost Shifting of Negative Externalities Lands Mostly on Those Least Able to Afford It
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-7444455625812656148" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.trbimg.com/img-547e40a7/turbine/la-mexico-farm-labor-camps-inline-barbed-wire-20141202/767/3x2/" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="266" src="http://www.trbimg.com/img-547e40a7/turbine/la-mexico-farm-labor-camps-inline-barbed-wire-20141202/767/3x2/" width="400"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://graphics.latimes.com/product-of-mexico-camps/">
                           Photo from the LA Times
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      From a heart-wrenching LA Times story on Mexican farm laborers,
                      <a href="http://graphics.latimes.com/product-of-mexico-camps/">
                       here's the rest of the price of the cheap food
                      </a>
                      --the part you're not paying:
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <ul>
                        <li>
                         Many farm laborers are essentially trapped for months at a time in rat-infested camps, often without beds and sometimes without functioning toilets or a reliable water supply.
                        </li>
                        <li>
                         Some camp bosses illegally withhold wages to prevent workers from leaving during peak harvest periods.
                        </li>
                        <li>
                         Laborers often go deep in debt paying inflated prices for necessities at company stores. Some are reduced to scavenging for food when their credit is cut off. It’s common for laborers to head home penniless at the end of a harvest.
                        </li>
                        <li>
                         Those who seek to escape their debts and miserable living conditions have to contend with guards, barbed-wire fences and sometimes threats of violence from camp supervisors.
                        </li>
                        <li>
                         Major U.S. companies have done little to enforce social responsibility guidelines that call for basic worker protections such as clean housing and fair pay practices.
                        </li>
                       </ul>
                      </blockquote>
                      Erik Loomis has
                      <a href="http://www.lawyersgunsmoneyblog.com/2014/12/grows-food">
                       an answer
                      </a>
                      :
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       If wages are stolen, workers threatened, bathing facilities not provided, etc., then workers should have the right to sue for recompense in American courts. Subway, Safeway, McDonald’s, etc., must be held legally responsible for the conditions of work when people labor in growing food for them to sell.
                      </blockquote>
                      If the food is cheap, someone paid something along the way--a subsidy paid by someone--that made it cheap. Either someone got underpaid, or had to work in horrible conditions, or some pollution went into the environment that causes someone illness or death. If we don't allow that to happen in this country, then why do we allow it to happen in some other country if that other country is shipping the product to us?
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Next time someone tries to sell you one of these so-called free trade pacts, ask them about the cost shifting. If
                      <i>
                       you're
                      </i>
                      not paying,
                      <i>
                       someone
                      </i>
                      is.
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Saturday, December 06, 2014
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://icestories.exploratorium.edu/dispatches/wp-content/uploads/2008/04/house_falling_over.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="1627876717146847672" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="1627876717146847672">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2014/12/romans-spent-years-building-nero-spent.html">
                       Romans Spent Years Building, Nero Spent a Few Hours Fiddling
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-1627876717146847672" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://icestories.exploratorium.edu/dispatches/wp-content/uploads/2008/04/house_falling_over.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="240" src="http://icestories.exploratorium.edu/dispatches/wp-content/uploads/2008/04/house_falling_over.jpg" width="320"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          A
                          <a href="http://icestories.exploratorium.edu/dispatches/big-ideas/climate-change/">
                           different kind of crumbling
                          </a>
                          being ignored by the GOP.
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      I'm sure Nero's fiddling sounded something like
                      <a href="http://thehill.com/policy/finance/225820-gop-chairman-obama-has-worst-record-on-debt">
                       this
                      </a>
                      :
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "[Obama has] the worst record of any president when it comes to putting America deeper in debt.”--Republican National Committee chairman Reince Priebus
                      </blockquote>
                      Steve Benen﻿
                      <a href="http://www.msnbc.com/rachel-maddow-show/rncs-priebus-picks-the-wrong-fight-the-wrong-issue">
                       does his usual great job
                      </a>
                      chipping through that old outcropping of bullshit.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       ...just last week, congressional Republicans pushed for a package of tax breaks that would cost $440 billion over the next decade. How would GOP lawmakers pay for this? They wouldn’t...
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       President Obama has overseen the fastest deficit reduction seen in the United States since the end of World War II. For that matter, nearly all of the president’s agenda – Affordable Care Act, immigration reform, etc. – would actually improve the nation’s finances.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       ...turned a massive surplus into a massive deficit, putting two wars, two tax breaks, Medicare expansion, and a Wall Street bailout on the national charge card, leaving the bill for future generations.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       ...public debt grew under Reagan – who promised as a candidate to balance the federal budget – by 186%.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       ...H.W. Bush increased the debt by 55%, Clinton by 37% (he’s the only modern president to see surpluses), W. Bush by 86%, and Obama by 59%.
                      </blockquote>
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                       <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-OFcPTw8jBrk/VINmdAxHYSI/AAAAAAAAIdk/_y9jHZoR9O8/s1600/US-Debt-chart.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;">
                        <img border="0" height="400" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-OFcPTw8jBrk/VINmdAxHYSI/AAAAAAAAIdk/_y9jHZoR9O8/s1600/US-Debt-chart.jpg" width="296"/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      Benen doesn't even mention that most of the debt accumulation under Obama can be laid squarely at the feet of GW Bush, as shown by
                      <a href="http://www.cbpp.org/cms/?fa=view&amp;id=3849">
                       this well-known-outside-the-conservative-bubble chart
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      So, at a time when Republicans' precious free markets are screaming at us to invest in infrastructure (low fuel, materials, labor, and borrowing costs), we are, instead of borrowing and spending on infrastructure that more than pays for itself like any good CEO would do now, watching little corporate piss ants like Reince Preibus give millions of wingnuts a talking point to drop like a bomb while they run away from the real fight.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      But the frame is set that Democrats are free spenders, so the GOP looks thrifty while the country literally crumbles.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Tuesday, September 23, 2014
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://www.andyworthington.co.uk/wp-content/uploads/abughraibhood.gif" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="2023164301495201704" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="2023164301495201704">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2014/09/the-battle-of-ideas-was-lost-at-abu.html">
                       The Battle of Ideas Was Lost at Abu Ghraib
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2023164301495201704" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.andyworthington.co.uk/wp-content/uploads/abughraibhood.gif" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="400" src="http://www.andyworthington.co.uk/wp-content/uploads/abughraibhood.gif" width="301"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          This is the US losing the war of ideas.
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Or maybe
                      <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/greg-mitchell/66-years-ago-the-crime-of_b_922109.html">
                       Nagasaki
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-29321136">
                       BBC
                      </a>
                      : "Eight civilians, including three children, were reported to have died."
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://www.defense.gov/Transcripts/Transcript.aspx?TranscriptID=2870">
                       Donald Rumsfeld
                      </a>
                      : “We are capturing and killing a lot of terrorists. But we also have to think about the number of new ones that are being created, it seems to me, and the memo I wrote raised that question — how might we do that? How do we win that battle of ideas?”
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      My Grandfather was UDT in WWII. He came back to Hawaii from island hopping and saw a bunch of Japanese playing volleyball with their guards. He got mad and asked one of the guards what the hell they were doing being nice to them. The guard answered that once the Japanese saw that we weren't the devils they’d been told, they told us everything we needed to know from them.
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-footer">
                      <div class="post-footer-line post-footer-line-1">

                         </a>
                        </span>
                       </span>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Saturday, September 20, 2014
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://election.princeton.edu/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Senate_seat_history_with_strikezone_9sep2014.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="718402693236126191" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="718402693236126191">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2014/09/democrats-to-hold-senate-is-nice-long.html">
                       Democrats to Hold Senate is a Nice Long Shot If You Can Get It
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-718402693236126191" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://election.princeton.edu/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Senate_seat_history_with_strikezone_9sep2014.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="300" src="http://election.princeton.edu/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/Senate_seat_history_with_strikezone_9sep2014.jpg" width="400"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          The
                          <a href="http://election.princeton.edu/2014/09/09/senate-2014-the-election-day-model-nerd-version/">
                           Geeky Version of Senate 2014 Election Day Model
                          </a>
                          from Sam Wang
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      From the mixed up files of the
                      <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/ThingsIWishICouldBetOn">
                       #ThingsIWishICouldBetOn
                      </a>
                      , this year is serving up an excellent long shot: Democrats to retain control of the Senate. It's a long shot for a reason, of course. Gamblers, especially the right-leaning ones looking for confirmation bias, learned that Nate Silver has been right a lot (something many of them learned the hard way). Democrats have to defend more seats. Midterms go against the incumbent President. People prefer Republicans in times of terror threats Republicans drum up (shorter Lindsey Graham: We're all gunna die!), even though
                      <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/plum-line/wp/2014/09/19/maybe-republicans-should-run-on-sending-in-ground-troops/">
                       Republicans want to start another land war in Asia that the people supposedly don't want
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Because,
                      <a href="http://www.esquire.com/blogs/politics/About_War">
                       of course they do
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      So, the nerd war between Nate Silver and Sam Wang have been entertaining as a way to highlight the differences between their prediction methods, but as we approach election day,
                      <a href="http://fivethirtyeight.com/interactives/senate-forecast/">
                       Nate's model
                      </a>
                      looks less at the "special sauce" and more at the polls. Since Wang doesn't add any special sauce, the two models will start to agree more. And it's Nate's model that's moving into agreement with Sam's. In fact, 538 moved from 64% GOP to 53% GOP in 9 days.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      And
                      <a href="http://election.princeton.edu/2014/09/09/senate-2014-the-election-day-model-nerd-version/">
                       Wang's prediction is a 70% chance
                      </a>
                      of Democrats holding control of the Senate.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://sports.betfair.com/?mi=109528811&amp;ex=1&amp;q=US%20Senate">
                       Betfair is paying 16/5 odds for Democrats to hold 51 seats
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      In one of the play-money prediction markets I'm in, I'm getting Dems to control (VP breaking tie counts as control) at 23.4 a share (pays 100).
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      I made some money betting with the Princeton model at Intrade, and, of course, now that there's decent odds against Wang, I have no where to legally bet.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Figures.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Standard long shot warning applies: don't bet as much on long-shots, as you're already subjecting yourself to some long-shot bias. But in a showdown between Silver and Wang, my money, at least a small chunk of it, would go with Wang. So, a sizable chunk of my play money is.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Furthermore, the Democrats have an ace in the hole, or, more precisely, some jokers:
                      <a href="http://www.thedailybeast.com/articles/2014/09/20/how-long-can-the-republicans-hide-the-crazy.html">
                       pent up pressure building under the lid the GOP is trying to hold on top of their boiling pot of crazy
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       ...we are well positioned to see some of these candidates take a journey on the crazy train in the closing weeks of this election cycle. Why? Three reasons. First, the debates are coming up, and as we saw in 2012 with Mourdock, the more these people talk in an unscripted forum, the more likely the guano will ooze out.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Second, in the tighter races, the candidates are feeling the heat. Consequently, they may make an unforced error or try to offer some red meat to the far right hoping it brings their base out in what’s expected to be a low-turnout election.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Finally, there are some male Republican candidates for Senate, like Colorado’s Corey Gardner and North Carolina’s Thom Tillis, who are playing with dynamite. By that I mean they’ve decided to talk birth control thinking it can help them, but one slip up on this issue, and cue the “Republican war on women” headlines.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Any of these scenarios could be trouble for the GOP. And not just for the candidate who made the comment, but it could put Republicans on the defensive nationwide.
                      </blockquote>
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://thegops.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/joni-ernst.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="180" src="http://thegops.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/joni-ernst.jpg" width="320"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          The Sarah Palin of the cornfields,
                          <a href="http://www.theeverlastinggopstoppers.com/2014/06/iowa-candidate-u-s-senate-united-nations-coming-property-rights-video/">
                           via the Everlasting GOP Stoppers
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Dean Obeidallah lists his Final Four crazies most likely to blow, which includes noted nullification expert Joni Ernst, the GOP Senate candidate in Iowa, who's reached pressure cooker levels of pent up crazy.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Nate Cohn notes:
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       If all of the candidates currently leading in the polls go on to win, which is not at all assured with so many close races and still 45 days to go, then the party that wins two from the list of Iowa, Alaska and Kansas will win the Senate.
                      </blockquote>
                      With Kansans, despite polling problems, looking more and more like less is wrong with them (they had to learn the hard way that
                      <a href="http://www.cbpp.org/cms/index.cfm?fa=view&amp;id=4110.">
                       Republicans are what's the matter with them
                      </a>
                      ) and Alaska being a tossup like Iowa, it seems my long shot could be depending on Joni Ernst doing or saying something really crazy, and when it comes to corn-fed Republicans and the crazy, the long shot looks better than even money.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Tuesday, September 09, 2014
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://www.veteransnewsnow.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/bush-king-abdulah-of-saudi-arabia-holding-hands.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="2373844212997642361" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="2373844212997642361">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2014/09/ma-nishtana.html">
                       Ma Nishtana
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2373844212997642361" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.veteransnewsnow.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/bush-king-abdulah-of-saudi-arabia-holding-hands.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="226" src="http://www.veteransnewsnow.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/08/bush-king-abdulah-of-saudi-arabia-holding-hands.jpg" width="320"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          GW Bush palling around
                          <br/>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      The first line of The Four Questions song from the Passover Seder asks "Ma Nishtana?" Or, "What has changed?" The term is often used sarcastically to refer to something that someone thinks is new, but is actually not.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      So, I ask, in a more contemporary English translation, "This is different how?"
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       “There’s nothing in it about national security,” Walter Jones, a Republican congressman from North Carolina who has read the missing pages, contends. “It’s about the Bush Administration and its relationship with the Saudis.” Stephen Lynch, a Massachusetts Democrat, told me that the document is “stunning in its clarity,” and that it offers direct evidence of complicity on the part of certain Saudi individuals and entities in Al Qaeda’s attack on America.
                      </blockquote>
                      That's
                      <a href="http://www.newyorker.com/news/daily-comment/twenty-eight-pages">
                       Lawrence Wright in the New Yorker
                      </a>
                      ,
                      <a href="http://digbysblog.blogspot.com/2014/09/the-enemy-of-my-enemy-is-my-enemy.html">
                       via Digby
                      </a>
                      , on the Twenty-Eight Pages the Dubya administration removed from the 9-11 Report.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Here's
                      <a href="http://www.thedailybeast.com/articles/2014/06/14/america-s-allies-are-funding-isis.html">
                       Josh Roggin at the Daily Beast
                      </a>
                      with the answer to the question of why on earth doesn't Dick Cheney talk about who's backing the bad guys de jour:
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       The Islamic State of Iraq and Syria (ISIS), now threatening Baghdad, was funded for years by wealthy donors in Kuwait, Qatar, and Saudi Arabia, three U.S. allies that have dual agendas in the war on terror.
                      </blockquote>
                      Ma Nishtana?
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Meanwhile, occasionally, someone from the elite actually stands up and
                      <a href="http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/die-hard-director-john-mctiernan-731171">
                       tells us what all this palling around with fascists has gotten us
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "I can only plead with you to examine the current political and cultural works of my country [the U.S.]. We are in the hands of a terrible counterrevolution and a great reaction, a second Civil War sponsored by the same people that lost the first Civil War," the director said.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "And it has created a good president who is a prisoner of the White House who can do little beyond the ceremonial," McTiernan continued. "It has made, despite of what you may see on screens, a prison country, and I've had the pleasure of seeing what most people in our class are never allowed to see. I've seen the engine of the beast, it has given us a country with more prisoners than North Korea per capita, more policemen per capita than Germany in 1938. They have suspended trial by jury in most of America."
                      </blockquote>
                      Now there's a guy I hope keeps talking.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Thursday, June 19, 2014
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5Tyv1z4HoCc/U6NGp9YUctI/AAAAAAAAHHk/nwO2nKDGw6A/s1600/IMG_9691+(2).jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="3390062990261452668" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="3390062990261452668">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2014/06/good-to-go-local-and-organic.html">
                       Good to Go Local and Organic
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-3390062990261452668" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5Tyv1z4HoCc/U6NGp9YUctI/AAAAAAAAHHk/nwO2nKDGw6A/s1600/IMG_9691+(2).jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="240" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5Tyv1z4HoCc/U6NGp9YUctI/AAAAAAAAHHk/nwO2nKDGw6A/s1600/IMG_9691+(2).jpg" width="320"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          Turkey Canadian bacon grilled cheese with caramelized
                          <br/>
                          onions, arugula, and tomato.
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Long time readers know we're big fans of
                      <a href="http://organicgarden.blogspot.com/">
                       organic gardening
                      </a>
                      and organic and local food in general. Now that we live in a rural area surrounded by great organic farms, we've decided to put our money and effort where our mouths are: a small, take out restaurant that focuses on local and organic food:
                      <a href="http://goodtogocv.com/">
                       Good to Go
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      We've just begun the venture, so we're at the fundraising stage. Rather than trying to borrow all the money to start the business, or going to accredited investors through a crowd funding site, we've decided to sell a 20% interest in the soon-to-be-formed LLC to our friends, family, readers, and community. We see this as a chance for anyone who truly believes in the resiliency of the local and slow food movement to help us create more demand for our local farmers.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Shares are $100 each, and represent a 0.1% share of the company. After we've been in business a few quarters, we plan to start buying back the shares over a 5 year period. During that time, by law, the LLC must pay each co-owner (known as members in New York) their percent of the net profits.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://goodtogocv.com/">
                       Visit the Good to Go Organic and Local Food web site
                      </a>
                      , read the
                      <a href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/0B-6QmhbfyxghM0dIMVR5V081LWs/edit?usp=sharing">
                       business plan
                      </a>
                      , and decide for yourself. We're sure you'll see this as a great way for the slow, organic, and local food community to create more demand for food that gets eaten as close to where it's grown as possible. And while we're not getting too dreamy about the whole thing, we see this as a kind of co-op model for financing these kinds of ventures as an excellent opportunity for investors and those who want to do something similar.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      So, please,
                      <a href="http://goodtogocv.com/index.php/get-involved/">
                       get involved today
                      </a>
                      . We're also looking for suppliers of organic and local food in the Cherry Valley, Cooperstown, and Sharon Springs New York area. If you have any questions, just leave a comment, or contact me directly (scott at supak dot com).
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>
