                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Tuesday, June 03, 2014
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Sock_puppets.jpg/800px-Sock_puppets.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="743959199361649797" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="743959199361649797">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2014/06/the-great-intrade-sock-puppet-fire-of.html">
                       The Great Intrade Sock Puppet Fire of 2012
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-743959199361649797" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Sock_puppets.jpg/800px-Sock_puppets.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="173" src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Sock_puppets.jpg/800px-Sock_puppets.jpg" width="320"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Sock_puppets.jpg">
                           Photo by Bastique
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Seems
                      <a href="http://www.buzzfeed.com/maxseddon/documents-show-how-russias-troll-army-hit-america">
                       Putin's asymmetric war on public opinion may have been fought with an army of sock puppets
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Russia’s campaign to shape international opinion around its invasion of Ukraine has extended to recruiting and training a new cadre of online trolls that have been deployed to spread the Kremlin’s message on the comments section of top American websites.
                      </blockquote>
                      At Intrade in the spring and early summer of 2012, I was commenting regularly in the "Obama to win" market. For every liberal commenter, there would be at least ten "conservatives." I would get pounded with insults, Gish Gallops, every kind of fallacy in the book behind some of the most horrific arguments for terrible things you've ever heard of.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      It got so bad that Intrade changed the policy to only allow paid accounts (people actually funding their accounts for betting) to comment.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      It got so quiet all of a sudden that I still call it The Great Intrade Sock Puppet Fire of 2012.
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-WH3QOoy3V8g/UvqFj5PIjeI/AAAAAAAAGVI/K-umFXes23A/s1600/infrastructure+spending.png" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="6639342008369072731" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="6639342008369072731">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2014/02/gop-letting-it-all-crumble-because-they.html">
                       GOP Letting It All Crumble Because They Like Bombs Better Than Bridges
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6639342008369072731" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-WH3QOoy3V8g/UvqFj5PIjeI/AAAAAAAAGVI/K-umFXes23A/s1600/infrastructure+spending.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="320" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-WH3QOoy3V8g/UvqFj5PIjeI/AAAAAAAAGVI/K-umFXes23A/s1600/infrastructure+spending.png" width="258"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          The opposite of what we
                          <br/>
                          should be doing right now.
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/02/07/1275936/-Spending-down-deficits-halved-and-public-sector-smaller-since-Obama-took-office">
                       Government spending is down, deficits have been halved, and the public sector is smaller since Obama took office
                      </a>
                      . Of course, this is the opposite of what a Progressive government would be doing with so many people out of work and
                      <a href="http://www.infrastructurereportcard.org/">
                       so much infrastructure crumbling
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Democrats, especially progressive ones, but even the President (a moderate Democrat), have been pushing for more infrastructure spending. Republicans will not pass any. They won't even pass minimal funding for an Infrastructure Bank, which used to be a Bipartisan idea, supported by Former Senator Hutchison of Texas, for one.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Now they seem intent on letting our infrastructure, which makes us more productive, pays for itself, and helps keep American companies here, crumble.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      If terrorists were killing as many Americans as our crumbling infrastructure, I wonder how much Republicans would be willing to borrow and spend to invade and occupy a country that had nothing to do with it?
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Wednesday, December 18, 2013
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/sotc/service/global/map-percentile-mntp/201311.gif" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="1165827223880424774" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="1165827223880424774">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2013/12/the-planet-was-really-hot-last-month.html">
                       The Planet Was Really Hot Last Month and Damn Do I Miss Intrade
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-1165827223880424774" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                       <a href="http://data.giss.nasa.gov/gistemp/graphs_v3/Fig.C.gif" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;">
                        <br/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                       <a href="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/sotc/service/global/map-percentile-mntp/201311.gif" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;">
                        <img border="0" height="246" src="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/sotc/service/global/map-percentile-mntp/201311.gif" width="320"/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      <a href="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/sotc/global/2013/11">
                       November was record warm
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       The combined average temperature over global land and ocean surfaces for November 2013 was record highest for the 134-year period of record, at 0.78°C (1.40°F) above the 20th century average of 12.9°C (55.2°F).
                      </blockquote>
                      The November monthly GISS temperature anomaly was
                      <a href="http://data.giss.nasa.gov/gistemp/tabledata_v3/GLB.Ts+dSST.txt">
                       0.77 above the 1951-1980 base period used by Intrade
                      </a>
                      , where I was buying the monthly GISS temperature anomaly to be more than 0.75 C for 25 cents a share (binary market, pays off $10).
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      If I bet the same amount of money 39 months in a row and lost, then a win in the 40th would cover all my losses. I started betting at Intrade in Dec 2011. So, now it is 24 months and I would have had a win. At that rate, one is almost doubling one's money, with a guarantee of higher rates of return if one understands that temperatures are rising.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://data.giss.nasa.gov/gistemp/graphs_v3/Fig.C.gif" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em; text-align: center;">
                       <img border="0" height="206" src="http://data.giss.nasa.gov/gistemp/graphs_v3/Fig.C.gif" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                      Considering the enthusiasm of the deniers over their (unskewed) "pause" and the amount of time it had been since an anomaly over .75, I could have been paying even less than 25 cents per share for the over 0.75 market.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Too bad the
                      <a href="http://amciv.com/contest">
                       American Civics Exchange contest
                      </a>
                      (which I won the $1000 second prize in last month) won't be doing climate markets... But if you want to join and make political and economic predictions, go play! Use my user name "supak" when you sign up; I think I still have a few thousand in bonus play money to collect for signing people up.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Wednesday, November 27, 2013
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://img689.imageshack.us/img689/3263/plutocracy.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="7599530830652646165" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="7599530830652646165">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2013/11/never-been-confirmed-by-facts-piling-on.html">
                       Never Been Confirmed by the Facts: Piling on the Trickle Downers
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-7599530830652646165" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://img689.imageshack.us/img689/3263/plutocracy.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="380" src="http://img689.imageshack.us/img689/3263/plutocracy.jpg" width="400"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.economicpopulist.org/content/chart-worshipers-part-swappers-and-inequality">
                           From the Economic Populist
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Guess who said this:
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Some people continue to defend trickle-down theories which assume that economic growth, encouraged by a free market, will inevitably succeed in bringing about greater justice and inclusiveness in the world.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       This opinion, which has never been confirmed by the facts, expresses a crude and naive trust in the goodness of those wielding economic power and in the sacra­lized workings of the prevailing economic system.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Meanwhile, the excluded are still waiting.
                      </blockquote>
                      <br/>
                      Nope, not me. Not Paul Krugman. Not Jared Bernstein. Not Dean Baker.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      It's
                      <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/business/economy/pope-francis-denounces-trickle-down-economic-theories-in-critique-of-inequality/2013/11/26/e17ffe4e-56b6-11e3-8304-caf30787c0a9_story.html?hpid=z1">
                       Pope Francis
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Now, if the Pope can see through the right wing bullshit and say something publicly against it, I think he might want to start riding around in that bullet proof Popemobile.
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Saturday, October 26, 2013
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://edwardjayepstein.com/2002image/netherpopup.gif" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="4385442377463079323" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="4385442377463079323">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2013/10/donald-rumsfeld-said-bin-ladens.html">
                       Donald Rumsfeld Said Bin Laden's Mountain Lair was Serious Business
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-4385442377463079323" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://edwardjayepstein.com/2002image/netherpopup.gif" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="400" src="http://edwardjayepstein.com/2002image/netherpopup.gif" width="355"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://edwardjayepstein.com/nether_fictoid3.htm">
                           The fictoid of Bin Laden's mountain fortress
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Paul Waldman has a great piece that will defibrillate your memory of
                      <a href="http://prospect.org/article/dick-cheney-still-thinks-he-was-character-24">
                       the kind of BS that was coming out of the Bush-Cheney administration after they got caught with their pants down
                      </a>
                      --after W himself had told the CIA agent that gave him the PDB on August 6, 2001 entitled
                      <i>
                       <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bin_Ladin_Determined_To_Strike_in_US">
                        Bin Laden Determined to Strike in US
                       </a>
                       ,
                      </i>
                      "
                      <a href="http://www.salon.com/2006/06/20/911pdb/">
                       All right. You've covered your ass, now.
                      </a>
                      "
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Here's a paragraph and the footnote from Paul:
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       The answer, in case you've forgotten, is that [Cheney] and so many other Bush administration officials were basically enacting a fantasy in which the enemy—"the terrorists"—were not actually a bunch of semi-literate religious fanatics who got incredibly lucky one time with an extraordinarily low-tech attack, but were actually evil geniuses, had unlimited resources at their disposal, and could execute complex, highly technical schemes with multiple interlocking parts that enabled them to do things like get close enough to the Vice President to deliver him a fatal electric shock. And of course, we can't close Guantanamo and house the prisoners now there in supermax prisons in the United States, from which no inmate has ever escaped, because they're terrorists, and who knows what super-powers they might have developed in the fantastically well-equipped lab in their hollowed-out-mountain lair?
                       <span style="color: #333333; font-family: 'Droid Serif', Cambria, Georgia, 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-size: 16px; line-height: 26px;">
                       </span>
                       <span class="sidenotenumber" style="border: 0px; color: #990000; font-family: 'Droid Sans', Calibri, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, 'Lucida Grande', Verdana, sans-serif !important; font-size: 12px !important; font-weight: bold; line-height: 26px; margin: 0px; padding: 0px; position: relative; top: -0.5em; vertical-align: baseline;">
                        1
                       </span>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <span style="color: #990000; font-family: 'Droid Sans', Calibri, 'Helvetica Neue', Arial, Helvetica, 'Lucida Grande', Verdana, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-weight: bold; line-height: 20px;">
                        1
                       </span>
                       I joke, but do you remember Bin Laden's mountain fortress? It was quite a remarkable feat of engineering—check out
                       <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sEJe5l_ELSA">
                        this conversation
                       </a>
                       between Tim Russert and Donald Rumsfeld, going over all its amazing details. "A ventilation system!" marveled Russert. "The entrances large enough to drive trucks and even tanks!" Even computer systems and telephone systems. It's a very sophisticated operation!" "Oh, you bet," responded the Secretary of Defense. "This is serious business. And there's not one of those. There are many of them." You may also remember that the mountain fortress never existed. It was all made up.
                      </blockquote>
                      It's amazing alright. Go read
                      <a href="http://edwardjayepstein.com/nether_fictoid3.htm">
                       the story of how this particular piece of bullshit made it out of Rumsfeld's mouth
                      </a>
                      ,  from Edward J Epstein, and how, perhaps even more horrifying, the press ate it up.
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Monday, October 21, 2013
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://ir-na.amazon-adsystem.com/e/ir?t=scottsupakbaldmo&amp;l=as2&amp;o=1&amp;a=B005H5O20C" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="145173708770656097" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="145173708770656097">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2013/10/from-conversation-on-political.html">
                       From a Conversation on Political Philosophy: The Conservative Infatuation with The Violence of Empire and Inequality
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-145173708770656097" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      </div>
                      I highly recommend this
                      <a href="http://thenewinquiry.com/features/redefining-the-right-wing/">
                       conversation between Corey Robin and Daniel Larison
                      </a>
                      . Maybe now I'll get off my lazy ass and order Robin's book,
                      <i>
                       <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B005H5O20C/ref=as_li_qf_sp_asin_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=B005H5O20C&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=scottsupakbaldmo">
                        The Reactionary Mind: Conservatism from Edmund Burke to Sarah Palin
                       </a>
                       <img alt="" border="0" height="1" src="http://ir-na.amazon-adsystem.com/e/ir?t=scottsupakbaldmo&amp;l=as2&amp;o=1&amp;a=B005H5O20C" style="border: none !important; margin: 0px !important;" width="1"/>
                      </i>
                      . Maybe it will stir up distant memories from philosophy classes that will make me better understand the underpinnings of today's conservatives. After reading Robin's blogging for years, I'm certain I'll learn something.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      I took a few notes while reading the riveting conversation, when I wasn't busy looking up topics like pan-Slavism, which I had forgotten about. Mostly I was interested in Larison's apparent embarrassment in regards to the right's infatuation with violence.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Daniel Larison: "...there is no disputing that most conservatives in most Western countries in the past two centuries have supported their governments’ foreign wars. I am still not persuaded that this is because there is a conservative infatuation with violence. There are several other factors that may help account for it: deference to authority"
                      </blockquote>
                      If authority is violent, and you defer to it, is this not an infatuation w/ violence? Is deferring to violence not support for it? If they're not infatuated with the violence (and I think they are, based on how many times I heard "nuke all Muslims" during debates about Iraq), then they are infatuated with the perpetrators of violence. So infatuated, in fact, that rather than think through the conservative implications of imperialism, they not only defer to the violent authority, but they use violence against those who oppose it.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      I was physically attacked many times by people who got angry that they couldn't argue with me about the war. I was attacked a few times by people who attempted to make a coherent argument for the Iraq war, but found themselves floundering to the point that they had to resort to throwing a punch. I argued with conservatives and some neo-liberals, some of them in my own family, and was eventually told that either I should support my president in a time of war, or I was a traitor. This seems more like "the distorting effects of nationalism" Larison lists as another possible explanation for the tendency for violence on the right, but if someone allows nationalism to distort their view to such an extent as to accuse someone of treason (punishable by death), doesn't this expose an infatuation with violence that is tempered only by a desire not to get one's hands bloody?
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      To this day, I hear people try to defend the Iraq war (mostly lame arguments involving the "everyone thought they had WMD" BS, which isn't really a defense but a spreading of blame). Is this infatuation with defending the violent Bush administration not itself an infatuation with violence? If not directly, then indirectly through continued support for those who committed it?
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Corey Robin: "the primary audience for violence on the right is the perpetrator and/or his/her allies. In other words, the right sees violence as primarily a source of rejuvenation among a ruling class that has gone soft. "
                      </blockquote>
                      Is this not the best explanation for the support of GW Bush's
                      <a href="http://costsofwar.org/iraq-10-years-after-invasion">
                       $6 trillion dollar war
                      </a>
                      ? And even if you don't think the "deference to authority" is, in itself, violence, then isn't the right's continued defense of the Iraq war a result of the primary audience for violence on the right being the allies of the perpetrator? Isn't the right's continued defense of Iraq an attempt to milk every last ounce of rejuvenation from the violence in order to toughen up the right that has, supposedly, gone soft?
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      It reminds me of the Lee Atwater quote about the southern strategy (the
                      <a href="http://www.thenation.com/article/170841/exclusive-lee-atwaters-infamous-1981-interview-southern-strategy">
                       audio
                      </a>
                      of which was recently released). He says that you start of saying "nigger, nigger" in order to get votes for the GOP in the south, and then that starts to backfire, so you start talking about bussing, taxes, more "abstract" things that still, essentially, say "nigger, nigger!" In this case, it's hippie punching. Right wingers still want to punch hippies, and many of them still do, but that kind of lashing out tends to backfire, makes you look bad. So, now you're talking about opposing a violent, power crazed President who's lying us into a war, you must be a traitor who would be toast in any other country, so you should surrender to the power of the authority that knows what's good for you. It's certainly more abstract than a right cross to the nose, but the infatuation with violence has merely gone from actually throwing the punch oneself, to wishing that the powerful authority to which one defers would put you to death for your non-Patriotic use of the 1st Amendment. Just because your hands don't have blood on them doesn't mean you're not violent. It just means you don't like the mess, so you defer to an authority--a kind of outsourcing of the violence.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      I often think of how, when he was running for office, GW Bush used the phrase "compassionate conservatism." Is the continued defense of the Bush administration, with a gaping lack of reference to compassion, and a continued reliance on the idea of spreading democracy at the barrel of a gun, not the  toughening up of a philosophy that many on the right saw as "too soft." Is not the current fervor to stop people from getting affordable insurance, or to cut food stamps, or to cut minorities off from the voting booth, or to blame the 47% who are moochers for all our problems, aren't these all methods to "toughen up" the right? Aren't these all just more abstract ways of punching hippies?
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Larison: "If we assume that concentrating wealth and increasing economic inequality were goals of the right, I suppose I would have to agree that there has been success of a sort. But I don’t consider either of those things to be desirable or consistent with conservative assumptions."
                      </blockquote>
                      If economic inequality were not goals of the right, then what is trickle down economics? Are we to believe that conservatives actually believed that if we cut taxes on the rich that would lead to more economic equality? And since Larison admitted earlier that a large part of conservatism is deference to authority, then isn't having more wealth in the hands of the supposedly deserving meritocracy an outcome the right would desire?
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Anyway, great conversation. Very educational.
                      <a href="http://thenewinquiry.com/features/redefining-the-right-wing/">
                       Go read the whole thing
                      </a>
                      .
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Saturday, October 19, 2013
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://cdn.theatlantic.com/static/mt/assets/jamesfallows/DeficitChart.png" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="934417294468154561" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="934417294468154561">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2013/10/wingnuts-say-obama-has-exploded-us-debt.html">
                       Wingnuts Say Obama Has Exploded US Debt Which Is, Unfortunately, Wrong
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-934417294468154561" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://cdn.theatlantic.com/static/mt/assets/jamesfallows/DeficitChart.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="400" src="http://cdn.theatlantic.com/static/mt/assets/jamesfallows/DeficitChart.png" width="387"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          Source:
                          <a href="http://www.cbpp.org/cms/index.cfm?fa=view&amp;id=3490">
                           Center on Budget and Policy Priorities
                          </a>
                          analysis
                          <br/>
                          based on CBO estimates.
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      The more I listen to elected Republicans, who, thank goodness,
                      <a href="http://keeptalkingwingnuts.blogspot.com/">
                       just won't stop talking
                      </a>
                      , the more I realize that they're
                      <a href="http://press.princeton.edu/titles/7929.html">
                       bullshitters
                      </a>
                      . They must know basic facts like the size of US deficits and debt. They must know that the deficit is falling. They must know that the current debt cannot, in any honest economic sense of the word, be blamed on President Obama. But they don't care. They have an impression they want to make, so they don't care what's true and what's not. They just say whatever they have to say in order to convey the impression they want to make, which is, of course, that Democrats are big borrowers and spenders, and they are the party of fiscal responsibility.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Of course, anyone with even a loose grasp of facts knows why this is bullshit. But, apparently, some people still need help with the facts. So, occasionally, I set people straight. It's especially fun to set wingnuts straight, although it gets old when you point out how wrong they are, and they just disappear, only to come back some other day with more bullshit that shows that they just ignored the actual facts.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Today, I see that
                      <a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/news/2013-10-18/the-tea-party-by-the-numbers.html">
                       Bloomberg has a poll that illustrates this break with reality that Tea Party Republicans have suffered
                      </a>
                      , and continue to suffer, because they believe the BS from the people they elected. They allow the impression being made by the bullshitters to take root in their walled off minds, and they pick and choose the information they need to feed that impression until it festers into a boil that sorely needs to be lanced. If only they weren't so afraid of needles.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Two-thirds of regular Republicans believe the federal budget deficit has grown this year and 93 percent of Tea Party Republicans agree. Both are wrong; the budget deficit is
                       <a href="http://www.bloomberg.com/news/2013-05-14/u-s-deficit-to-fall-to-642-billion-says-budget-agency.html">
                        projected to fall
                       </a>
                       this year from $1.1 trillion to $642 billion.
                      </blockquote>
                      That's just this year. Go back a ways, and their delusion gets even stronger. For example, tell them Obama has cut the deficit in half since he took office from GW Bush, and they often become apoplectic, if they don't just leave and avoid the subject. They'll wail about how Obama sent the deficit soaring to such heights that even he could keep it up.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      So, the real kicker is when you show them what the money is for. Like any good bullshitter, they'll say I'm a weak, pathetic libtard for blaming Bush. When the truth is, for centuries in this country, those described as weak and pathetic were the ones who knowingly chose to believe fantasy over reality. I'm looking at you, Confederate States of America.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      The chart at the top of this post lists the sources of the current deficits that are adding to our debt. It is a stark reminder of the fact that any Republican who claims they are the party of limited government is bullshitting you and will probably ask for a campaign contribution right after doing so. The entire GOP has become a country club of con artists, and their base is the mark.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://zfacts.com/sites/all/files/image/debt/US-national-debt-GDP.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="286" src="http://zfacts.com/sites/all/files/image/debt/US-national-debt-GDP.png" width="400"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          Source:
                          <a href="http://zfacts.com/p/318.html">
                           ZFacts
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      The chart at the right is the one that should be shoved in the face of any bullshitting wingnut who dares to suggest that Republicans are the party of fiscal responsibility. And note that anyone capable of putting chart A and chart B together will realize that the debt spike under Obama is really legacy spending from that codpiece wearing hero of the Mission Accomplished wingnuts, GW Bush, from his wars (
                      <a href="http://costsofwar.org/iraq-10-years-after-invasion">
                       the Iraq war will eventually cost over $6 trillion
                      </a>
                      ), his tax cuts (which we were told would create millions of jobs and resulted in
                      <a href="http://blogs.wsj.com/economics/2009/01/09/bush-on-jobs-the-worst-track-record-on-record/">
                       the worst job creation record on record
                      </a>
                      ), TARP (started by Bush and finished by Obama, but only necessary because of Bush), recovery measures from the Little Bush Depression (like the stimulus, which was
                      <a href="http://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/statements/2010/feb/10/jon-stewart/stewart-claims-stimulus-bill-one-third-tax-cuts/">
                       one-third tax cuts
                      </a>
                      , something
                      <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2010/10/19/us/politics/19taxes.html">
                       Republicans refuse to believe
                      </a>
                      ), and the reduced revenues due to the Little Bush Depression.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      One last fact to keep in mind on this last graph: When calculating debt as a percent of GDP, it's important to remember that GW Bush's final GDP, in 4Q2008, was
                      <a href="http://www.economist.com/blogs/freeexchange/2011/08/fiscal-policy#">
                       negative 9%
                      </a>
                      . When GDP spikes down like that, and emergency spending goes up (job losses were at 800,000 per month when Obama took office and  in the three months before the stimulus passed, the economy cut loose 2.2m workers), the debt as a percent of GDP will, of course, go up. To blame that on Obama is the ultimate in bullshit.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/wonkblog/files/2013/02/Fixed-investment.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="240" src="http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/wonkblog/files/2013/02/Fixed-investment.png" width="400"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          "Private fixed investment as a percentage of potential GDP.
                          <br/>
                          When it gets back to historical norms, the free lunch
                          <br/>
                          on infrastructure investment will be over."
                          <br/>
                          <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/wonkblog/wp/2013/02/11/is-congress-really-going-to-miss-its-free-lunch-on-infrastructure/">
                           Neil Irwin
                          </a>
                          ,
                          <i>
                           Washington Post
                          </i>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      What this whole argument misses is that cutting the deficit right now is the worst thing to do. We should be be doing what the
                      <a href="http://cpc.grijalva.house.gov/the-peoples-budget/">
                       Congressional Progressive Caucus's People's Budget
                      </a>
                      would do: borrow more at currently low interest rates, buy cheap materials, and put unemployed people back to work fixing our
                      <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/wonkblog/wp/2013/02/11/is-congress-really-going-to-miss-its-free-lunch-on-infrastructure/">
                       crumbling infrastructure
                      </a>
                      , which would more than pay for itself. This won't happen, of course, as long as the GOP controls the House. But if they keep spewing their bullshit, and enough people learn the truth, maybe we can extend the
                      <a href="http://election.princeton.edu/2013/10/17/how-long-will-the-shutdowns-effect-on-opinion-last/">
                       half life of their polling plunge
                      </a>
                      , take advantage of the
                      <a href="http://election.princeton.edu/2013/10/17/house-2014-election-analysis-errors-not-mine-i-think/">
                       hidden weakness of gerrymandering
                      </a>
                      , and then keep the bullshitters talking long enough to replace them with some people who want to put this country back to work.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Tuesday, October 08, 2013
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="http://images2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100714055310/westwing/images/9/97/Cj_ashland.png" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="3104306" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="7025997749982602713" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="7025997749982602713">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://supak.blogspot.com/2013/10/scalia-is-right-wings-version-of-west.html">
                       Scalia Is the Right Wing's Version of the West Wing's Justice Roy Ashland
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-7025997749982602713" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://images2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100714055310/westwing/images/9/97/Cj_ashland.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" src="http://images2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100714055310/westwing/images/9/97/Cj_ashland.png"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          Fictional Chief Justice of the Supreme Court
                          <a href="http://westwing.wikia.com/wiki/Roy_Ashland">
                           Roy Ashland
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      In season five of
                      <i>
                       The West Wing
                      </i>
                      , the great Irish actor
                      <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0642675/">
                       Milo O'Shea
                      </a>
                      played aging Supreme Court Justice
                      <a href="http://westwing.wikia.com/wiki/Roy_Ashland">
                       Roy Ashland
                      </a>
                      , whose mental deterioration had the White House worried when he wrote an opinion in
                      <a href="http://www.westwingtranscripts.com/search.php?flag=getTranscript&amp;id=81">
                       trochiac tetrometer
                      </a>
                      . I'd have loved to see the reaction in the west wing to
                      <a href="http://nymag.com/news/features/antonin-scalia-2013-10/index.html">
                       Justice Antonin Scalia's interview in
                       <i>
                        New York Magazine
                       </i>
                      </a>
                      today.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "...power tends to corrupt."
                      </blockquote>
                      Lack of self-awareness can be a sign denial (in his case, projection), or some worse problem, like anosognosia.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "If Congress can get its act together, it can roll over the president. That’s what the framers thought. They said you have to enlist your jealousy against the legislature in a ¬democracy—that will be the source of tyranny."
                      </blockquote>
                      I don't disagree, but I wonder if he thinks the logic applies to his branch enlisting its jealousy against the legislature? When he says one thing, then does another, the hypocrisy appears to be politically motivated, and he just sounds like the Bullshitter he is. But perhaps his logical inconsistencies and lack of self awareness have really been flare ups from an undiagnosed condition?
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Here he is on the Defense of Marriage Act, in his dissent in
                      <i>
                       US v Windsor
                      </i>
                      :
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "We have no power to decide this case. And even if we did, we have no power under the Constitution to invalidate this democratically adopted legislation."
                      </blockquote>
                      This is precisely the opposite of his opinion (joining Roberts) in Shelby County, Alabama v Holder, where he joined in striking down Section 4 of the Voting Rights Act, which had been reauthorized by a near-unanimous Congress.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Of course, Jennifer Senior doesn't follow up with any questions about this glaring inconsistency in the long interview. Damn liberal media being so mean to him and all... can't be too tough or conservatives won't agree to interviews (looking at you, Jon Stewart, Bill Maher, et al)...
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      This guy is such a stouthearted originalist that "cruel and unusual" punishment does not include flogging, so of course being put in jail for butt sex is fine.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "...if a state enacted a law permitting flogging, it is immensely stupid, but it is not unconstitutional. A lot of stuff that’s stupid is not unconstitutional. I gave a talk once where I said they ought to pass out to all federal judges a stamp, and the stamp says—Whack! [Pounds his fist.]—STUPID BUT ¬CONSTITUTIONAL. Whack! [Pounds again.] STUPID BUT ¬CONSTITUTIONAL! Whack! ¬STUPID BUT ¬CONSTITUTIONAL … [Laughs.] And then somebody sent me one."
                      </blockquote>
                      Someone please ask Justin A. Frank to write
                      <i>
                       Scalia on the Couch
                      </i>
                      next. I'd like to know more about the proximity of his affinity for flogging and his pounding of his fist to mimic the stamping motion.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Just how stout is this stouthearted originalist?
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        What about sex discrimination? Do you think the Fourteenth Amendment covers it?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Of course it covers it! No, you can’t treat women differently, give them higher criminal sentences. Of course not.
                      </blockquote>
                      He tries to weasel a little as to why he's given a different answer on that before. Fact is, the people who passed the 14th didn't have women in mind. The Supremes themselves determined that the 14th did not apply to women in Minor v. Happersett (more accurately, that decision claimed voting was not a constitutional right). It took the 19th Amendment to overturn that "originalist" decision. Go read the whole article to watch him contort himself into defending unequal treatment of women as NOT discrimination, like prohibiting women from combat. I'd have loved to hear him expand on that list, but alas, onward we must go, because Liberal Media!
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "You can’t go to a movie—or watch a television show for that matter—without hearing the constant use of the F-word—including, you know, ladies using it."
                      </blockquote>
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="https://si0.twimg.com/profile_images/1312892893/scalia-gesture.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" src="https://si0.twimg.com/profile_images/1312892893/scalia-gesture.jpg"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          We all know what
                          <a href="http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=5312065">
                           this gesture
                          </a>
                          means
                          <br/>
                          here in the US, Antonin.
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Scalia thinks ladies saying fuck is more coarsening to society than
                      <a href="http://thinkprogress.org/justice/2013/02/27/1646891/scalia-voting-rights-act-is-perpetuation-of-racial-entitlement/">
                       his words on the Voting Rights Act
                      </a>
                      :
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       And this last enactment, not a single vote in the Senate against it. And the House is pretty much the same. Now, I don’t think that’s attributable to the fact that it is so much clearer now that we need this. I think it is attributable, very likely attributable, to a phenomenon that is called perpetuation of racial entitlement. It’s been written about. Whenever a society adopts racial entitlements, it is very difficult to get out of them through the normal political processes.
                      </blockquote>
                      My Italian wife says "Fuck you, Tony."
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Here's Justice Scalia's contribution to a less coarse society:
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        The one thing I did think, as he said those somewhat welcoming things to gay men and women, is, Huh, this really does show how much our world has changed. I was wondering what kind of personal exposure you might have had to this sea change.
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       I have friends that I know, or very much suspect, are homosexual. Everybody does.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        Have any of them come out to you?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       No. No. Not that I know of.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        Has your personal attitude softened some?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Toward what?
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        Homosexuality.
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       I don’t think I’ve softened. I don’t know what you mean by softened.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        If you talk to your grandchildren, they have different opinions from you about this, right?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       I don’t know about my grandchildren. I know about my children. I don’t think they and I differ very much. But I’m not a hater of homosexuals at all.
                      </blockquote>
                      Evasive much? But note that Scalia's son also doesn't exactly
                      <i>
                       hate
                      </i>
                      homosexuals,
                      <a href="http://www.rightwingwatch.org/content/scalias-son-says-homosexuality-doesnt-exist-plans-address-group-encourages-lifelong-abstinen">
                       he just denies they exist
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Maybe Scalia and his son do differ, and Scalia believes homosexuals exist. His comment ("I have friends that I know, or very much suspect, are homosexual") seems to suggest that he thinks they exist. So there's a big difference with his son.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      The obvious point is that when Scalia says he doesn't hate homosexuals, it seems to not fit with his desire to declare sodomy laws constitutional (
                      <i>
                       Lawrence v. Texas
                      </i>
                      ). It does not fit with his desire to allow states to deny gay couples marriage rights. But even if we don't look at his record, we can just see
                      <a href="http://www.motherjones.com/politics/2013/03/scalia-worst-things-said-written-about-homosexuality-court">
                       what he's said about homosexuals
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      He joked about sodomy laws being like laws about flag pole sitting. He suggested that laws banning homosexual sex were like laws against murder. He suggested they were like laws banning child porn, incest, and bestiality. But he doesn't hate you, gay people, so relax. It's not like he thinks you're the work of the devil.
                      <br/>
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.perditionreport.com/ninthcircle/wp-content/uploads/2012/01/Flanders-Satan.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="320" src="http://www.perditionreport.com/ninthcircle/wp-content/uploads/2012/01/Flanders-Satan.jpg" width="253"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          <br/>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        Can we talk about your drafting process—
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       [Leans in, stage-whispers.] I even believe in the Devil.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        You do?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Of course! Yeah, he’s a real person. Hey, c’mon, that’s standard Catholic doctrine! Every Catholic believes that.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        Every Catholic believes this? There’s a wide variety of Catholics out there …
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       If you are faithful to Catholic dogma, that is certainly a large part of it.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        Have you seen evidence of the Devil lately?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       You know, it is curious. In the Gospels, the Devil is doing all sorts of things. He’s making pigs run off cliffs, he’s possessing people and whatnot. And that doesn’t happen very much anymore.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        No.
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       It’s because he’s smart.
                      </blockquote>
                      Smart like a homosexual fox. I wonder what Scalia would think of the proposition that
                      <a href="http://satanwrotethebible.com/">
                       the Devil is so smart he actually wrote the Bible
                      </a>
                      ? Maybe Satan has just gotten lazy and prefers to watch cable.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       I watched one episode of—what is it? Duck Dynasty?
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        What?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       I don’t watch it regularly, but I’m a hunter. I use duck calls …
                      </blockquote>
                      <a href="http://www.cbsnews.com/2100-250_162-607115.html">
                       We know
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       "It did not involve a lawsuit against Dick Cheney as a private individual," Scalia said in response to a question from the audience of about 600 people. "This was a government issue. It's acceptable practice to socialize with executive branch officials when there are not personal claims against them. That's all I'm going to say for now. Quack, quack."
                      </blockquote>
                      Later he says his statement refusing to recuse himself from Cheney's case was his most "heroic" opinion. Gotta get in a shout out to his partner in crime. Maybe Scalia would feel differently about hunting, and his old hunting partner, had Scalia gone on a different hunting trip with Cheney.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://media.salon.com/2012/06/scalia_rect2-620x412.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="212" src="http://media.salon.com/2012/06/scalia_rect2-620x412.jpg" width="320"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          Scalia's tell that he has a good hand. (Reuters/Yuri Gripas)
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Of course, it's next to impossible to interview what might be the biggest bullshitter in the country without accidentally exposing some
                      <a href="http://press.princeton.edu/titles/7929.html">
                       bullshit
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        Here’s another thing I find unexpected about you: that you play poker. Do not take this the wrong way, but you strike me as the kind of person who would be a horrible poker player.
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Shame on you! I’m a damn good poker player.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        But aren’t you the kind of guy who always puts all of his cards on the table? I feel like you would be the worst bluffer ever.
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       You can talk to the people in my poker set.
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <b>
                        Do you have a tell?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       What?
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        A tell.
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       What’s a tell?
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        What’s a tell? Are you joking?
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       No.
                      </blockquote>
                      <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;">
                       <tbody>
                        <tr>
                         <td style="text-align: center;">
                          <a href="http://www.advocate.com/sites/advocate.com/files/imagecache/stories/Antonin-ScaliaX400.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;">
                           <img border="0" height="240" src="http://www.advocate.com/sites/advocate.com/files/imagecache/stories/Antonin-ScaliaX400.jpg" width="320"/>
                          </a>
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                        <tr>
                         <td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">
                          Scalia with a bad hand. Getty Images,
                          <a href="http://www.advocate.com/politics/2013/07/22/scalia-judges-not-qualified-legislate-homosexual-sodomy">
                           via
                          </a>
                          .
                         </td>
                        </tr>
                       </tbody>
                      </table>
                      Hey, Antonin, how do I get in your poker set? I regret that I couldn't have played you before you learned what a "tell" is, but I'm thinking even knowing about such a thing won't stop you from having one.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      And, isn't gambling in DC, Virginia, and Maryland illegal? Can a Supreme Court justice be indicted? If he's convicted, can we replace him? Or do we have to watch him deteriorate in prison, while he decides cases from his cell?
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        But how will you know when it’s time to go? It doesn’t seem like you have anything to worry about at the moment, but it’s interesting to hear you even flick at that.
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       Oh, I’ll know when I’m not hitting on all eight cylinders.
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       <b>
                        Are you sure? All these people in ¬public life—athletes in particular—never have a clue.
                       </b>
                      </blockquote>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       No, I’ll know.
                      </blockquote>
                      Hopefully, he'll read this interview. But, even if he was aware that he's losing it, he most likely won't resign if there's a Democrat in the White House. I'm sure he figures even if he is losing it, he'd still be a better justice than his replacement.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://www.noisyroom.net/blog/respect.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em; text-align: center;">
                       <img border="0" height="200" src="http://www.noisyroom.net/blog/respect.jpg" width="200"/>
                      </a>
                      My proof for this? Just witness the level of narcissism already on display here in his praise for his heroic lone dissent in
                      <i>
                       Morrison v. Olson
                      </i>
                      , which declared the Independent Counsel Act constitutional.
                      <br/>
                      <blockquote class="tr_bq">
                       I care about the reasoning. And the reasoning in Morrison, I thought, was devastating—devastating of the majority. If you ask me which of my opinions will have the most impact in the future, it probably won’t be that dissent; it’ll be some majority opinion. But it’ll have impact in the future not because it’s so beautifully reasoned and so well written. It’ll have impact in the future because it’s authoritative. That’s all that matters, unfortunately.
                      </blockquote>
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                       <a href="http://www.noisyroom.net/blog/respect.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;">
                        <br/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      <i>
                       Respect My Authoritah!
                      </i>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Hopefully the literary scholars will team up with the lawyers and watch for any signs of trochiac tetrometer in Scalia's opinions from now on.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
